Federal city of Switzerland

**Bern** (
Swiss Standard German: [\[bɛrn\]](/wiki/Help:IPA/Standard_German "Help:IPA/Standard German") [](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/transcoded/1/1d/De-Bern.ogg/De-Bern.ogg.mp3 "Play audio")^[ⓘ](/wiki/File:De-Bern.ogg "File:De-Bern.ogg")^), or **Berne** (
French: [\[bɛʁn\]](/wiki/Help:IPA/French "Help:IPA/French") [](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/transcoded/f/f2/LL-Q150_%28fra%29-DSwissK-Berne.wav/LL-Q150_%28fra%29-DSwissK-Berne.wav.mp3 "Play audio")^[ⓘ](/wiki/File:LL-Q150_(fra)-DSwissK-Berne.wav "File:LL-Q150 (fra)-DSwissK-Berne.wav")^),^[\[note 1\]](#cite_note-3)^ is the *[de facto](/wiki/De_facto "De facto")* ^[\[note 2\]](#cite_note-DeFacto-4)^ [capital](/wiki/Capital_city "Capital city") of [Switzerland](/wiki/Switzerland "Switzerland"), referred to as the "[federal city](/wiki/Federal_city "Federal city")".^[\[note 3\]](#cite_note-5)^^[\[3\]](#cite_note-deFacto-6)^ With a population of about 146,000 (as of 2024^[\[update\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Bern&action=edit)^), Bern is the [fifth-most populous city in Switzerland](/wiki/List_of_cities_in_Switzerland "List of cities in Switzerland"), behind [Zürich](/wiki/Z%C3%BCrich "Zürich"), [Geneva](/wiki/Geneva "Geneva"), [Basel](/wiki/Basel "Basel") and [Lausanne](/wiki/Lausanne "Lausanne").^[\[4\]](#cite_note-StatBern-7)^ The Bern agglomeration, which includes 36 municipalities, had a population of 406,900 in 2014.^[\[5\]](#cite_note-Agglomeration-8)^ The [metropolitan area](/wiki/Metropolitan_area "Metropolitan area") had a population of 660,000 in 2000.^[\[6\]](#cite_note-9)^{#cite_ref-9}

Bern is also the capital of the [canton of Bern](/wiki/Canton_of_Bern "Canton of Bern"), the second-most populous of [Switzerland's cantons](/wiki/Cantons_of_Switzerland "Cantons of Switzerland"). The official language is [German](/wiki/German_language "German language"),^[\[note 4\]](#cite_note-10)^ but the main spoken language is the local variant of the [Alemannic](/wiki/Alemannic_German "Alemannic German") [Swiss German](/wiki/Swiss_German "Swiss German") dialect, [Bernese German](/wiki/Bernese_German "Bernese German"). In 1983, the [historic old town](/wiki/Old_City_(Bern) "Old City (Bern)") (in [German](/wiki/German_language "German language"): *Altstadt* ) in the centre of Bern became a [UNESCO](/wiki/UNESCO "UNESCO") [World Heritage Site](/wiki/World_Heritage_Site "World Heritage Site").^[\[7\]](#cite_note-11)^ It is notably surrounded by the [Aare](/wiki/Aare "Aare"), a major river of the [Swiss Plateau](/wiki/Swiss_Plateau "Swiss Plateau").{#cite_ref-11}

Although fortified settlements were established since antiquity, the medieval city proper was founded by the [Zähringer](/wiki/Z%C3%A4hringer "Zähringer") ruling family, probably in 1191 by [Berthold V, Duke of Zähringen](/wiki/Berthold_V,_Duke_of_Z%C3%A4hringen "Berthold V, Duke of Zähringen"). Bern was made a [free imperial city](/wiki/Free_imperial_city "Free imperial city") in 1218 and, in 1353, it joined the [Swiss Confederacy](/wiki/Old_Swiss_Confederacy "Old Swiss Confederacy"), becoming one of its eight early cantons. Since then, Bern became a large [city-state](/wiki/City-state "City-state") and a prominent actor of Swiss history by pursuing a policy of sovereign territorial expansion. Since the 15th century, the city was progressively rebuilt and acquired its current characteristics. Bern was made the [Federal City](/wiki/Federal_City "Federal City") in 1848. From about 5,000 inhabitants in the 15th century, the city passed the 100,000 mark in the 1920s.  

Etymology {#Etymology}
----------------------

\[[edit](/w/index.php?title=Bern&action=edit&section=1 "Edit section: Etymology")\]  
See also [Other names of Bern](/wiki/Names_of_European_cities_in_different_languages:_B "Names of European cities in different languages: B")

The etymology of the name "Bern" is uncertain. According to the local legend, based on [folk etymology](/wiki/Folk_etymology "Folk etymology"), [Berthold V, Duke of Zähringen](/wiki/Berthold_V,_Duke_of_Z%C3%A4hringen "Berthold V, Duke of Zähringen"), the founder of the city of Bern, vowed to name the city after the first animal he met on the hunt, and this turned out to be a bear. It has long been considered likely that the city was named after the Italian city of [Verona](/wiki/Verona "Verona"), which at the time was known as *Bern* in [Middle High German](/wiki/Middle_High_German "Middle High German"). The city was sometimes referred to as *Bern im [Üechtland](/wiki/%C3%9Cechtland "Üechtland")* to distinguish it from Verona.^[\[8\]](#cite_note-12)^ As a result of the finding of the [Bern zinc tablet](/wiki/Bern_zinc_tablet "Bern zinc tablet") in the 1980s, it is now more common to assume that the city was named after a pre-existing toponym of Celtic origin, possibly *\*berna* "cleft".^[\[9\]](#cite_note-13)^ The bear was the heraldic animal of the [seal and coat of arms of Bern](/wiki/Coat_of_arms_of_Bern "Coat of arms of Bern") from at least the 1220s. The earliest reference to the keeping of live bears in the *[Bärengraben](/wiki/B%C3%A4rengraben "Bärengraben")* dates to the 1440s.{#cite_ref-13}  

History {#History}
------------------

\[[edit](/w/index.php?title=Bern&action=edit&section=2 "Edit section: History")\]  
Main article: [History of Bern](/wiki/History_of_Bern "History of Bern")  
For a chronological guide, see [Timeline of Bern](/wiki/Timeline_of_Bern "Timeline of Bern").  

### Early history {#Early_history}

\[[edit](/w/index.php?title=Bern&action=edit&section=3 "Edit section: Early history")\]
[![](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f2/Untertorbr%C3%BCcke_Tschachtlanchronik.jpg/170px-Untertorbr%C3%BCcke_Tschachtlanchronik.jpg)](/wiki/File:Untertorbr%C3%BCcke_Tschachtlanchronik.jpg) Construction of the [Untertorbrücke](/wiki/Untertorbr%C3%BCcke "Untertorbrücke") (Lower Gate Bridge) in Bern, [Tschachtlanchronik](/wiki/Tschachtlanchronik "Tschachtlanchronik"), late 15th century

No [archaeological](/wiki/Archaeological "Archaeological") evidence that indicates a settlement on the site of today's city centre prior to the 12th century has been found so far. In antiquity, a [Celtic](/wiki/Celts "Celts") *[oppidum](/wiki/Oppidum "Oppidum")* stood on the *Engehalbinsel* (peninsula) north of Bern, fortified since the second century BC (late [La Tène period](/wiki/La_T%C3%A8ne_period "La Tène period")), thought to be one of the 12 *oppida* of the [Helvetii](/wiki/Helvetii "Helvetii") mentioned by [Caesar](/wiki/Commentarii_de_Bello_Gallico "Commentarii de Bello Gallico"). During the [Roman era](/wiki/Germania_Superior "Germania Superior"), a [Gallo-Roman](/wiki/Gallo-Roman "Gallo-Roman") *[vicus](/wiki/Vicus "Vicus")* was on the same site. The Bern zinc tablet has the name *Brenodor* ("dwelling of Breno"). In the Early Middle Ages, a settlement in [Bümpliz](/wiki/B%C3%BCmpliz "Bümpliz"), now a city district of Bern, was some 4 km (2 mi) from the medieval city.

The medieval city is a foundation of the [Zähringer](/wiki/Z%C3%A4hringer "Zähringer") ruling family, which rose to power in [Upper Burgundy](/wiki/Upper_Burgundy "Upper Burgundy") in the 12th century. According to 14th-century historiography (*Cronica de Berno* , 1309), Bern was founded in 1191 by [Berthold V, Duke of Zähringen](/wiki/Berthold_V,_Duke_of_Z%C3%A4hringen "Berthold V, Duke of Zähringen").

In 1218, after Berthold died without an heir, Bern was made a [free imperial city](/wiki/Free_imperial_city "Free imperial city") by the *[Goldene Handfeste](/wiki/Goldene_Handfeste "Goldene Handfeste")* of [Holy Roman Emperor](/wiki/Holy_Roman_Emperor "Holy Roman Emperor") [Frederick II](/wiki/Frederick_II,_Holy_Roman_Emperor "Frederick II, Holy Roman Emperor").  

### Old Swiss Confederacy {#Old_Swiss_Confederacy}

\[[edit](/w/index.php?title=Bern&action=edit&section=4 "Edit section: Old Swiss Confederacy")\]

In 1353, Bern joined the [Swiss Confederacy](/wiki/Old_Swiss_Confederacy "Old Swiss Confederacy"), becoming the eighth canton of the formative period of 1353 to 1481.

Bern invaded and conquered [Aargau](/wiki/Aargau "Aargau") in 1415 and [Vaud](/wiki/Vaud "Vaud") in 1536, as well as other smaller territories, thereby becoming the largest [city-state](/wiki/City-state "City-state") north of the [Alps](/wiki/Alps "Alps"). By the 18th century, it comprised most of what is today the [canton of Bern](/wiki/Canton_of_Bern "Canton of Bern") and the [canton of Vaud](/wiki/Canton_of_Vaud "Canton of Vaud").
[![](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/41/MerianBern.jpg/220px-MerianBern.jpg)](/wiki/File:MerianBern.jpg) Bern in 1638

The city grew out towards the west of the boundaries of the peninsula formed by the river [Aare](/wiki/Aare "Aare"). The *[Zytglogge](/wiki/Zytglogge "Zytglogge")* tower marked the western boundary of the city from 1191 until 1256, when the *Käfigturm* took over this role until 1345. It was succeeded by the *[Christoffelturm](/wiki/Christoffelturm "Christoffelturm")* (formerly located closer to the site of the modern-day railway station) until 1622. During the [Thirty Years' War](/wiki/Thirty_Years%27_War "Thirty Years' War"), two new fortifications -- the so-called big and small *[Schanze](/wiki/Schanze "Schanze")* (entrenchments) -- were built to protect the whole area of the peninsula.

After a major blaze in 1405, the city's original wooden buildings were gradually replaced by [half-timbered](/wiki/Half-timbered "Half-timbered") houses, and subsequently the [sandstone](/wiki/Sandstone "Sandstone") buildings which came to be characteristic for the Old Town. Despite waves of [pestilence](/wiki/Bubonic_plague "Bubonic plague") that hit Europe in the 14th century, the city continued to grow, mainly due to [immigration](/wiki/Immigration "Immigration") from the surrounding countryside.^[\[10\]](#cite_note-14)^{#cite_ref-14}

During the 18th century, the city of Bern was at one point the largest shareholder in the [South Sea Company](/wiki/South_Sea_Company "South Sea Company"), a British [joint-stock company](/wiki/Joint-stock_company "Joint-stock company") which was involved in the [Atlantic slave trade](/wiki/Atlantic_slave_trade "Atlantic slave trade").^[\[11\]](#cite_note-15)^ From 1689 to 3 March 1798 in the town was printed, in [French](/wiki/French_language "French language"), the biweekly newspaper *[Gazette de Berne](/wiki/Gazette_de_Berne "Gazette de Berne")* , which reflected the opinions of Bern,^[\[12\]](#cite_note-16)^ usually hostile to the politics of [Pre-revolutionary France](/wiki/Pre-revolutionary_France "Pre-revolutionary France").^[\[13\]](#cite_note-17)^{#cite_ref-17}  

### Modern history {#Modern_history}

\[[edit](/w/index.php?title=Bern&action=edit&section=5 "Edit section: Modern history")\]
[![](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f8/Johann_Heinrich_M%C3%BCller%2C_1825-1894_H01b_Bern.JPG/220px-Johann_Heinrich_M%C3%BCller%2C_1825-1894_H01b_Bern.JPG)](/wiki/File:Johann_Heinrich_M%C3%BCller,_1825-1894_H01b_Bern.JPG) Bern c. 1870.   
Etching by [Heinrich Müller](https://commons.wikimedia.org/wiki/Category:Johann_Heinrich_M%C3%BCller_(1825-1894) "commons:Category:Johann Heinrich Müller (1825-1894)")

Bern was occupied by [French](/wiki/First_French_Republic "First French Republic") troops in 1798 during the [French Revolutionary Wars](/wiki/French_Revolutionary_Wars "French Revolutionary Wars"), when it was stripped of parts of its territories. It regained control of the [Bernese Oberland](/wiki/Bernese_Oberland "Bernese Oberland") in 1802, and following the [Congress of Vienna](/wiki/Congress_of_Vienna "Congress of Vienna") of 1814, it newly acquired the [Bernese Jura](/wiki/Bernese_Jura "Bernese Jura"). At this time, it once again became the largest canton of the Confederacy as it stood during the [Restoration](/wiki/Restoration_(Switzerland) "Restoration (Switzerland)") and until the secession of the [canton of Jura](/wiki/Canton_of_Jura "Canton of Jura") in 1979.

On 28 November 1848, during the [revolutions that year](/wiki/Revolutions_of_1848 "Revolutions of 1848"), a majority of the new Swiss [Federal Assembly](/wiki/Federal_Assembly_of_Switzerland "Federal Assembly of Switzerland") deputies chose Bern as the [Federal City](/wiki/Federal_City "Federal City") (seat of the government) of the newly created [Swiss federal state](/wiki/Switzerland_as_a_federal_state "Switzerland as a federal state"), ahead of [Zürich](/wiki/Z%C3%BCrich "Zürich") and [Lucerne](/wiki/Lucerne "Lucerne"). Bern was chosen as not to concentrate all the power in the economic powerhouse of Zürich, while Catholic and conservative Lucerne had been part of the [Sonderbund](/wiki/Sonderbund_War "Sonderbund War") during the war a year before. In addition, Bern had a more central location and was supported by the French-speaking cantons due to proximity to them. However, the constitution doesn't define Bern as official capital of Switzerland, but as the seat of government.^[\[14\]](#cite_note-18)^{#cite_ref-18}

A number of congresses of the [socialist](/wiki/Socialist "Socialist") [First](/wiki/First_International "First International") and [Second Internationals](/wiki/Second_International "Second International") were held in Bern, particularly during [World War I](/wiki/World_War_I "World War I") when Switzerland was neutral; see [Bern International](/wiki/Bern_International "Bern International").

The city's population rose from about 5,000 in the 15th century to about 12,000 by 1800 and to above 60,000 by 1900, passing the 100,000 mark during the 1920s. Population peaked during the 1960s at 165,000 and has since decreased slightly, to below 130,000 by 2000. As of September 2017, the resident population stood at 142,349, of which 100,000 were Swiss citizens and 42,349 (31%) resident foreigners. A further estimated 350,000 people live in the immediate [urban agglomeration](/wiki/Urban_agglomeration "Urban agglomeration").^[\[15\]](#cite_note-19)^{#cite_ref-19}  

Geography and climate {#Geography_and_climate}
----------------------------------------------

\[[edit](/w/index.php?title=Bern&action=edit&section=6 "Edit section: Geography and climate")\]  

### Topography {#Topography}

\[[edit](/w/index.php?title=Bern&action=edit&section=7 "Edit section: Topography")\]  
Further information: [List of parks in Bern](/wiki/List_of_parks_in_Bern "List of parks in Bern")
[![](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/75/Bern_luftaufnahme.png/220px-Bern_luftaufnahme.png)](/wiki/File:Bern_luftaufnahme.png) Aerial view of the [Old City of Bern](/wiki/Old_City_of_Bern "Old City of Bern") and the [Aare](/wiki/Aare "Aare") [![](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fe/Bern_2.jpg/220px-Bern_2.jpg)](/wiki/File:Bern_2.jpg) The Old City with the Minster and its platform above the lower *Matte* quarter and the [Aare](/wiki/Aare "Aare") [![](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0d/Aareschlaufe_Bern-East.svg/220px-Aareschlaufe_Bern-East.svg.png)](/wiki/File:Aareschlaufe_Bern-East.svg) The Aare flows in a wide loop around the Old City. [![](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/39/Bern%2C_Switzerland.JPG/220px-Bern%2C_Switzerland.JPG)](/wiki/File:Bern,_Switzerland.JPG) View of Bern from the [ISS](/wiki/International_Space_Station "International Space Station"). The Old City is on the lower right-hand side.

Bern lies on the [Swiss plateau](/wiki/Swiss_plateau "Swiss plateau") in the canton of Bern, slightly west of the centre of Switzerland and 20 km (12 mi) north of the [Bernese Alps](/wiki/Bernese_Alps "Bernese Alps"). The countryside around Bern was formed by glaciers during the most recent [ice age](/wiki/Ice_age "Ice age"). The two mountains closest to Bern are [Gurten](/wiki/Gurten_(mountain) "Gurten (mountain)") with a height of 864 m (2,835 ft) and [Bantiger](/wiki/Bantiger "Bantiger") with a height of 947 m (3,107 ft). The site of the old observatory in Bern is the point of origin of the [CH1903 coordinate system](/wiki/Swiss_coordinate_system "Swiss coordinate system") at [46°57′08.66″N 7°26′22.50″E﻿ / ﻿46.9524056°N 7.4395833°E﻿ / 46.9524056; 7.4395833](https://geohack.toolforge.org/geohack.php?pagename=Bern&params=46_57_08.66_N_7_26_22.50_E_region:CH_type:landmark).

The city was originally built on a hilly [peninsula](/wiki/Peninsula "Peninsula") surrounded by the river [Aare](/wiki/Aare "Aare"), but outgrew natural boundaries by the 19th century. A [number of bridges](/wiki/List_of_Aar_bridges_in_Bern "List of Aar bridges in Bern") have been built to allow the city to expand beyond the Aare.

Bern is built on very uneven ground. An elevation difference of up to 60 metres exists between the inner city districts on the Aare ([Matte](/wiki/Mattequartier "Mattequartier"), [Marzili](/w/index.php?title=Marzili,_Bern&action=edit&redlink=1 "Marzili, Bern (page does not exist)")) and the higher ones (Kirchenfeld, Länggasse).

Bern has an area, as of 2013^[\[update\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Bern&action=edit)^, of 51.62 km^2^ (19.93 sq mi). Of this area, 9.42 km^2^ (3.64 sq mi) or 18.2% is used for agricultural purposes, while 17.21 km^2^ (6.64 sq mi) or 33.3% is forested. Of the rest of the land, 23.76 km^2^ (9.17 sq mi) or 46.0% is settled (buildings or roads), 1.08 km^2^ (0.42 sq mi) or 2.1% is either rivers or lakes, and 0.14 km^2^ (0.054 sq mi) or 0.3% is unproductive land.^[\[16\]](#cite_note-BFS_land-20)^{#cite_ref-BFS_land_20-0}

Of the developed area of Bern, 3.1% consists of industrial buildings, 22.3% housing and other buildings, and 12.9% is devoted to transport infrastructure. Power and water infrastructure, as well as other special developed areas, made up 1.2% of the city, while another 6.5% consists of parks, green belts, and sports fields.

Of Bern's total land area, 32.8% is heavily forested. Of the agricultural land, 13.3% is used for growing crops and 4.4% is designated to be used as pasture. Local rivers and streams provide all the water in the municipality.^[\[16\]](#cite_note-BFS_land-20)^{#cite_ref-BFS_land_20-1}
[![](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/ce/ETH-BIB-Bern%2C_M%C3%BCnster-Bern-Inlandfl%C3%BCge-LBS_MH01-000191.tif/lossy-page1-220px-ETH-BIB-Bern%2C_M%C3%BCnster-Bern-Inlandfl%C3%BCge-LBS_MH01-000191.tif.jpg)](/wiki/File:ETH-BIB-Bern,_M%C3%BCnster-Bern-Inlandfl%C3%BCge-LBS_MH01-000191.tif) Aerial view by [Walter Mittelholzer](/wiki/Walter_Mittelholzer "Walter Mittelholzer") (1919)  

### Climate {#Climate}

\[[edit](/w/index.php?title=Bern&action=edit&section=8 "Edit section: Climate")\]

According to the [Köppen Climate Classification](/wiki/K%C3%B6ppen_Climate_Classification "Köppen Climate Classification"), Bern has an [oceanic climate](/wiki/Oceanic_climate "Oceanic climate") (*Cfb* )^[\[17\]](#cite_note-:0-21)^ closely bordering on a [humid continental climate](/wiki/Humid_continental_climate "Humid continental climate") (*Dfb*).{#cite_ref-:0_21-0}

The closest weather station near Bern is located in the municipality of [Zollikofen](/wiki/Zollikofen "Zollikofen"), about 5 kilometres (3 mi) north of the city centre. The warmest month for Bern is July, with a daily mean temperature of 18.3 °C (64.9 °F), and a daily maximum temperature of 24.3 °C (75.7 °F).^[\[17\]](#cite_note-:0-21)^ The highest temperature recorded at Bern / Zollikofen is 37.0 °C (98.6 °F),^[\[18\]](#cite_note-22)^ recorded in [August 2003](/wiki/2003_European_heat_wave "2003 European heat wave"). On average, a temperature of 25 °C (77 °F) or above is recorded 40.7 days per year, and 6 days per year with a temperature of 30 °C (86 °F) or above at Zollikofen,^[\[17\]](#cite_note-:0-21)^ and the warmest day reaches an average of 32.1 °C (89.8 °F).^[\[19\]](#cite_note-23)^{#cite_ref-23}

There are 103.7 days of air frost, and 22.3 ice days per year at Bern (Zollikofen) for the period of 1981--2010, as well as 14.1 days of snowfall, 36.7 days of snow cover per year and the average amount of snow measured per year is 52.6 centimetres (20.7 in).^[\[17\]](#cite_note-:0-21)^ On average, January is the coldest month, with a daily mean temperature of −0.4 °C (31.3 °F), and a daily minimum temperature of −3.6 °C (25.5 °F).^[\[17\]](#cite_note-:0-21)^ The lowest temperature ever recorded at Bern (Zollikofen) was −23.0 °C (−9.4 °F),^[\[20\]](#cite_note-24)^ recorded in February 1929, and typically the coldest temperature of the year reaches an average of −12.8 °C (9.0 °F)^[\[21\]](#cite_note-25)^ for the period of 1981--2010.{#cite_ref-25}  
{#cite_ref-NOAA1_26-0}{#cite_ref-28}

\[[edit](/w/index.php?title=Bern&action=edit&section=9 "Edit section: Politics")\]  

### Subdivisions {#Subdivisions}

\[[edit](/w/index.php?title=Bern&action=edit&section=10 "Edit section: Subdivisions")\]

The municipality is administratively subdivided into six districts (*Stadtteile* ), each of which consists of several quarters (*Quartiere*).

### Government {#Government}

\[[edit](/w/index.php?title=Bern&action=edit&section=11 "Edit section: Government")\]
[![](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e4/Erlacherhof.jpg/220px-Erlacherhof.jpg)](/wiki/File:Erlacherhof.jpg) Erlacherhof [![](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/37/Rathaus_%28Bern%29.jpg/220px-Rathaus_%28Bern%29.jpg)](/wiki/File:Rathaus_(Bern).jpg) Rathaus  
See also: [List of mayors of Bern](/wiki/List_of_mayors_of_Bern "List of mayors of Bern")  
See also: [Gemeinderat (Bern)](/wiki/Gemeinderat_(Bern) "Gemeinderat (Bern)")

The Municipal Council (de: **Gemeinderat** , fr: **conseil municipal** ) constitutes the [executive](/wiki/Executive_(government) "Executive (government)") government of the City of Bern and operates as a [collegiate authority](/w/index.php?title=Collegiate_authority&action=edit&redlink=1 "Collegiate authority (page does not exist)"). It is composed of five councillors ([German](/wiki/German_language "German language"): *Gemeinderat/-rätin* , [French](/wiki/French_language "French language"): *conseiller/conseillère municipal(e)* ), each presiding over a directorate (de: *Direktion* , fr: *direction* ) comprising several departments and bureaus. The president of the executive department acts as [mayor](/wiki/Mayor "Mayor") (de: *Stadtpräsident/-präsidentin* , fr: *Le Maire* ). In the mandate period (*Legislatur* ) 2025--2028, the Municipal Council is presided by *Stadtpräsidentin* [Marieke Kruit](/w/index.php?title=Marieke_Kruit&action=edit&redlink=1 "Marieke Kruit (page does not exist)") \[[de](https://de.wikipedia.org/wiki/Marieke_Kruit "de:Marieke Kruit")\]. Departmental tasks, coordination measures and implementation of laws decreed by the City Council are carried by the Municipal Council. The regular election of the Municipal Council by any inhabitant valid to vote is held every four years. Any resident of Bern allowed to vote can be elected as a member of the Municipal Council. Contrary to most other municipalities, the executive government in Bern is selected by means of a system of [Proporz](/wiki/Proportional_representation "Proportional representation"). The mayor is elected as such as well by public election while the heads of the other directorates are assigned by the collegiate. The executive body holds its meetings in the [Erlacherhof](/wiki/Junkerngasse "Junkerngasse"), built by architect [Albrecht Stürler](/w/index.php?title=Albrecht_St%C3%BCrler&action=edit&redlink=1 "Albrecht Stürler (page does not exist)") after 1747.

As of 2025^[\[update\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Bern&action=edit)^, Bern's Municipal Council is made up of two representatives of the SP ([Social Democratic Party](/wiki/Social_Democratic_Party_of_Switzerland "Social Democratic Party of Switzerland")), and one each of GFL (*Grüne Freie Liste* a.k.a. Green Free List), GB ([Green Alliance of Bern](/w/index.php?title=Gr%C3%BCnes_B%C3%BCndnis_Bern&action=edit&redlink=1 "Grünes Bündnis Bern (page does not exist)")) and GLP ([Green Liberal Party](/wiki/Green_Liberal_Party_of_Switzerland "Green Liberal Party of Switzerland")), giving the left parties a very strong majority of four out of five seats. The last regular election was held on 24 November 2024.^[\[25\]](#cite_note-election-29)^ ^[\[26\]](#cite_note-GR-30)^{#cite_ref-GR_30-0}
{#cite_ref-31}{#cite_ref-32}

### Parliament {#Parliament}

\[[edit](/w/index.php?title=Bern&action=edit&section=12 "Edit section: Parliament")\]  
‹ The [template](/wiki/Help:Template "Help:Template") *[Pie chart](/wiki/Template:Pie_chart "Template:Pie chart")* is being [considered for merging](/wiki/Wikipedia:Templates_for_discussion/Log/2025_January_30#Template:Pie_chart "Wikipedia:Templates for discussion/Log/2025 January 30"). ›  
The *Stadtrat* of Bern for the mandate period of 2021--2024:^[\[29\]](#cite_note-SR-35)^{#cite_ref-SR_35-0}  
PdA (1.25%)  
AL (3.75%)  
GaP (1.25%)  
JUSO (2.5%)  
SP/PS (26.25%)  
JA! (3.75%)  
GB (12.5%)  
GFL (8.75%)  
jglp (2.5%)  
glp/pvl (11.25%)  
EVP/PEV (2.5%)  
CVP/PDC (2.5%)  
BDP/PBD (2.5%)  
FDP/PLR (8.75%)  
JF / DL (1.25%)  
SVP/UDC (8.75%)

The City Council (de: **Stadtrat** , fr: **Conseil de ville** ) holds [legislative power](/wiki/Legislative_power "Legislative power"). It is made up of 80 members, with elections held every four years. The City Council decrees regulations and by-laws that are executed by the Municipal Council and the administration. The delegates are selected by means of a system of [proportional representation](/wiki/Proportional_representation "Proportional representation").

The sessions of the City Council are public. Unlike members of the Municipal Council, members of the City Council are not politicians by profession, and they are paid a fee based on their attendance. Any resident of Bern allowed to vote can be elected as a member of the City Council. The parliament holds its meetings in the *Stadthaus* (Town Hall).

The last regular election of the City Council was held on 29 November 2020 for the mandate period ([German](/wiki/German_language "German language"): *Legislatur* , [French](/wiki/French_language "French language"): *la législature* ) from 2021 to 2024. The City Council consist of 23 (-1) members of the [Social Democratic Party (SP/PS)](/wiki/Social_Democratic_Party_of_Switzerland "Social Democratic Party of Switzerland") including two seats by the junior party *JUSO* , 11 (+3) [Green Liberal Party (glp/pvl)](/wiki/Green_Liberal_Party_of_Switzerland "Green Liberal Party of Switzerland") including two member of its junior party *jglp* , 10 (+1) [Green Alliance of Bern (GB)](/w/index.php?title=Gr%C3%BCnes_B%C3%BCndnis_Bern&action=edit&redlink=1 "Grünes Bündnis Bern (page does not exist)"), 8 (-1) [The Liberals (FDP/PLR)](/wiki/FDP.The_Liberals "FDP.The Liberals") including one seat by its junior partner *JF / DL* , 7 (-2) [Swiss People's Party (SVP/UDC)](/wiki/Swiss_People%27s_Party "Swiss People's Party"), 7 (-1) *Grüne Freie Liste (GFL)* (Green Free List), 3 (+1) *Junge Alternative (JA!)* (or Young Alternatives), 3 (+1) [Alternative Linke Bern (AL)](/wiki/Alternative_Left "Alternative Left"), 2 (-1) [Conservative Democratic Party (BDP/PBD)](/wiki/Conservative_Democratic_Party_of_Switzerland "Conservative Democratic Party of Switzerland"), 2 (-) [Christian Democratic People's Party (CVP/PDC)](/wiki/Christian_Democratic_People%27s_Party_of_Switzerland "Christian Democratic People's Party of Switzerland"), 2 (-) [Evangelical People's Party (EVP/PEV)](/wiki/Evangelical_People%27s_Party_of_Switzerland "Evangelical People's Party of Switzerland"), 1 (-) [Swiss Party of Labour (PdA)](/wiki/Swiss_Party_of_Labour "Swiss Party of Labour"), and 1 *Grüne alternative Partei (GaP)* (or Green alternative Party).^[\[25\]](#cite_note-election-29)^^[\[29\]](#cite_note-SR-35)^{#cite_ref-SR_35-1}  

### National elections {#National_elections}

\[[edit](/w/index.php?title=Bern&action=edit&section=13 "Edit section: National elections")\]  

#### National Council {#National_Council}

\[[edit](/w/index.php?title=Bern&action=edit&section=14 "Edit section: National Council")\]

In the [2019 federal election](/wiki/2019_Swiss_federal_election "2019 Swiss federal election") for the [Swiss National Council](/wiki/National_Council_(Switzerland) "National Council (Switzerland)") the most popular party was the [PS](/wiki/Social_Democratic_Party_of_Switzerland "Social Democratic Party of Switzerland") which received 28.7% (-5.6) of the vote. The next five most popular parties were the [Green Party](/wiki/Green_Party_of_Switzerland "Green Party of Switzerland") (25.2%, +7.9), the [pvl](/wiki/Green_Liberal_Party_of_Switzerland "Green Liberal Party of Switzerland") (13.5%, +4.1), the [UDC](/wiki/Swiss_People%27s_Party "Swiss People's Party") (9.5%, -2.9), [PLR](/wiki/FDP.The_Liberals "FDP.The Liberals") (4.2%, -2.8), and the [BDP/PBD](/wiki/Conservative_Democratic_Party_of_Switzerland "Conservative Democratic Party of Switzerland") (7.0%).^[\[30\]](#cite_note-36)^ In the federal election a total of 49,030 votes were cast, and the [voter turnout](/wiki/Voter_turnout "Voter turnout") was 56%.^[\[31\]](#cite_note-37)^{#cite_ref-37}

In the [2015 federal election](/wiki/2015_Swiss_federal_election "2015 Swiss federal election") for the [Swiss National Council](/wiki/National_Council_(Switzerland) "National Council (Switzerland)") the most popular party was the [PS](/wiki/Social_Democratic_Party_of_Switzerland "Social Democratic Party of Switzerland") which received 34.3% of the vote. The next five most popular parties were the [Green Party](/wiki/Green_Party_of_Switzerland "Green Party of Switzerland") (17.4%), the [UDC](/wiki/Swiss_People%27s_Party "Swiss People's Party") (12.4%), and the [FDP/PLR](/wiki/FDP.The_Liberals "FDP.The Liberals") (9.9%), [glp/pvl](/wiki/Green_Liberal_Party_of_Switzerland "Green Liberal Party of Switzerland") (9.4%), and the [BDP/PBD](/wiki/Conservative_Democratic_Party_of_Switzerland "Conservative Democratic Party of Switzerland") (7.0%). In the federal election, a total of 48,556 voters were cast, and the [voter turnout](/wiki/Voter_turnout "Voter turnout") was 56.0%.^[\[32\]](#cite_note-38)^{#cite_ref-38}  

### International relations {#International_relations}

\[[edit](/w/index.php?title=Bern&action=edit&section=15 "Edit section: International relations")\]  

#### Twin and sister cities {#Twin_and_sister_cities}

\[[edit](/w/index.php?title=Bern&action=edit&section=16 "Edit section: Twin and sister cities")\]

The Municipal Council of the city of Bern decided against having twinned cities except for a temporary (during the [UEFA Euro 2008](/wiki/UEFA_Euro_2008 "UEFA Euro 2008")) cooperation with the [Austrian](/wiki/Austria "Austria") city [Salzburg](/wiki/Salzburg "Salzburg").^[\[33\]](#cite_note-39)^^[\[34\]](#cite_note-40)^{#cite_ref-40}

|------|---------|--------|
| Source: ^[\[35\]](#cite_note-41)^^[\[36\]](#cite_note-42)^ |||
[Historical population]

Bern has a population (as of December 2020^[\[update\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Bern&action=edit)^) of 134,794.^[\[37\]](#cite_note-Stat2020_BE-43)^ About 34% of the population are resident foreign nationals. Over the 10 years between 2000 and 2010, the population changed at a rate of 0.6%. Migration accounted for 1.3%, while births and deaths accounted for −2.1%.^[\[38\]](#cite_note-SFSO-44)^{#cite_ref-SFSO_44-0}

Most of the population (as of 2000^[\[update\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Bern&action=edit)^) speaks German (104,465 or 81.2%) as their first language, Italian is the second most common (5,062 or 3.9%) and French is the third (4,671 or 3.6%). There are 171 people who speak [Romansh](/wiki/Romansh_language "Romansh language").^[\[39\]](#cite_note-STAT2000-45)^{#cite_ref-STAT2000_45-0}

As of 2008^[\[update\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Bern&action=edit)^, the population was 47.5% male and 52.5% female. The population was made up of 44,032 Swiss men (35.4% of the population) and 15,092 (12.1%) non-Swiss men. There were 51,531 Swiss women (41.4%) and 13,726 (11.0%) non-Swiss women.^[\[40\]](#cite_note-BE_Stat-46)^ Of the population in the municipality, 39,008 or about 30.3% were born in Bern and lived there in 2000. There were 27,573 or 21.4% who were born in the same canton, while 25,818 or 20.1% were born somewhere else in Switzerland, and 27,812 or 21.6% were born outside of Switzerland.^[\[39\]](#cite_note-STAT2000-45)^{#cite_ref-STAT2000_45-1}
[![](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3a/Bern_Bethlehem2.jpg/220px-Bern_Bethlehem2.jpg)](/wiki/File:Bern_Bethlehem2.jpg) Apartment blocks at Bern-Bethlehem

As of 2000^[\[update\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Bern&action=edit)^, children and teenagers (0--19 years old) make up 15.1% of the population, while adults (20--64 years old) make up 65% and seniors (over 64 years old) make up 19.9%.^[\[38\]](#cite_note-SFSO-44)^{#cite_ref-SFSO_44-1}

As of 2000^[\[update\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Bern&action=edit)^, there were 59,948 people who were single and never married in the municipality. There were 49,873 married individuals, 9,345 widows or widowers and 9,468 individuals who are divorced.^[\[39\]](#cite_note-STAT2000-45)^{#cite_ref-STAT2000_45-2}
[![](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bd/Houses_in_the_Old_City_of_Bern.jpg/220px-Houses_in_the_Old_City_of_Bern.jpg)](/wiki/File:Houses_in_the_Old_City_of_Bern.jpg) Houses in the Old City of Bern

As of 2000^[\[update\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Bern&action=edit)^, there were 67,115 private households in the municipality, and an average of 1.8 persons per household.^[\[38\]](#cite_note-SFSO-44)^ There were 34,981 households that consist of only one person and 1,592 households with five or more people. In 2000^[\[update\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Bern&action=edit)^, a total of 65,538 apartments (90.6% of the total) were permanently occupied, while 5,352 apartments (7.4%) were seasonally occupied and 1,444 apartments (2.0%) were empty.^[\[41\]](#cite_note-Housing-47)^ As of 2009^[\[update\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Bern&action=edit)^, the construction rate of new housing units was 1.2 new units per 1000 residents.^[\[38\]](#cite_note-SFSO-44)^{#cite_ref-SFSO_44-3}

As of 2003^[\[update\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Bern&action=edit)^ the average price to rent an average apartment in Bern was 1108.92 [Swiss francs](/wiki/Swiss_franc "Swiss franc") (CHF) per month (US$890, £500, €710 approx. exchange rate from 2003). The average rate for a one-room apartment was 619.82 CHF (US$500, £280, €400), a two-room apartment was about 879.36 CHF (US$700, £400, €560), a three-room apartment was about 1040.54 CHF (US$830, £470, €670) and a six or more room apartment cost an average of 2094.80 CHF (US$1680, £940, €1340). The average apartment price in Bern was 99.4% of the national average of 1116 CHF.^[\[42\]](#cite_note-BFS_rent-48)^ The vacancy rate for the municipality, in 2010^[\[update\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Bern&action=edit)^, was 0.45%.^[\[38\]](#cite_note-SFSO-44)^{#cite_ref-SFSO_44-4}

### Religion {#Religion}

\[[edit](/w/index.php?title=Bern&action=edit&section=19 "Edit section: Religion")\]
[![](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0c/Heiliggeistkirche_Bern_2.jpg/220px-Heiliggeistkirche_Bern_2.jpg)](/wiki/File:Heiliggeistkirche_Bern_2.jpg) Church of the Holy Spirit in Bern

From the 2000 census^[\[update\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Bern&action=edit)^, 60,455 or 47.0% belonged to the [Swiss Reformed Church](/wiki/Swiss_Reformed_Church "Swiss Reformed Church"), while 31,510 or 24.5% were members of the [Catholic Church](/wiki/Catholic_Church "Catholic Church"). Of the rest of the population, there were 1,874 [members of an Orthodox church](/wiki/Orthodoxy#Christianity "Orthodoxy") (or about 1.46% of the population), there were 229 persons (or about 0.18% of the population) who belonged to the [Christ Catholic Church](/wiki/Christian_Catholic_Church_of_Switzerland "Christian Catholic Church of Switzerland"), and there were 5,531 persons (or about 4.30% of the population) who belonged to another Christian religion. There were 324 persons (or about 0.25% of the population) who were [Jewish](/wiki/Jewish "Jewish"), and 4,907 (or about 3.81% of the population) who were [Muslim](/wiki/Muslim "Muslim"). There were 629 persons who were [Buddhist](/wiki/Buddhism "Buddhism"), 1,430 persons who were [Hindu](/wiki/Hinduism "Hinduism") and 177 persons who belonged to another religion. 16,363 (or about 12.72% of the population) belonged to no religion, are agnostic or [atheist](/wiki/Atheism "Atheism"), and 7,855 persons (or about 6.11% of the population) did not answer the question.^[\[39\]](#cite_note-STAT2000-45)^ On 14 December 2014 the [Haus der Religionen](/wiki/Haus_der_Religionen "Haus der Religionen") was inaugurated.{#cite_ref-STAT2000_45-3}  

Main sights {#Main_sights}
--------------------------

\[[edit](/w/index.php?title=Bern&action=edit&section=20 "Edit section: Main sights")\]
[![](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/45/Bundeshaus_Bern_2009%2C_Flooffy.jpg/220px-Bundeshaus_Bern_2009%2C_Flooffy.jpg)](/wiki/File:Bundeshaus_Bern_2009,_Flooffy.jpg) The central building of the Federal Palace of Switzerland [![](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/eb/4377_-_Bern_-_Kindlifresserbrunnen_am_Kornhausplatz.JPG/100px-4377_-_Bern_-_Kindlifresserbrunnen_am_Kornhausplatz.JPG)](/wiki/File:4377_-_Bern_-_Kindlifresserbrunnen_am_Kornhausplatz.JPG) The Ogre of the Kindlifresserbrunnen has a sack of children waiting to be devoured.

The structure of Bern's [city centre](/wiki/Old_City_(Bern) "Old City (Bern)") is largely [medieval](/wiki/Medieval "Medieval") and has been recognised by [UNESCO](/wiki/UNESCO "UNESCO") as a Cultural [World Heritage Site](/wiki/World_Heritage_Site "World Heritage Site"). Perhaps its most famous sight is the *[Zytglogge](/wiki/Zytglogge "Zytglogge")* (Bernese German for "Time Bell"), an elaborate medieval clock tower with moving puppets. It also has an impressive 15th century [Gothic](/wiki/Gothic_architecture "Gothic architecture") cathedral, the *[Münster](/wiki/M%C3%BCnster_(Bern) "Münster (Bern)")*, and a 15th-century town hall. Thanks to 6 kilometres (4 miles) of arcades, the old town boasts one of the longest covered shopping promenades in Europe.

Since the 16th century, the city has had a bear pit, the *[Bärengraben](/wiki/B%C3%A4rengraben "Bärengraben")* , at the far end of the [Nydeggbrücke](/wiki/Nydeggbr%C3%BCcke "Nydeggbrücke") to house its heraldic animals. The four bears are now kept in an open-air enclosure nearby, and two other young bears, a present by the Russian president, are kept in [Dählhölzli](/wiki/D%C3%A4hlh%C3%B6lzli "Dählhölzli") zoo.^[\[44\]](#cite_note-50)^{#cite_ref-50}

The Federal Palace ([Bundeshaus](/wiki/Federal_Palace_of_Switzerland "Federal Palace of Switzerland")), built from 1857 to 1902, which houses the [national parliament](/wiki/Swiss_Federal_Assembly "Swiss Federal Assembly"), government and part of the federal administration, can also be visited.

[Albert Einstein](/wiki/Albert_Einstein "Albert Einstein") lived in a flat at the [Kramgasse](/wiki/Kramgasse "Kramgasse") 49, the site of the [Einsteinhaus](/wiki/Einsteinhaus "Einsteinhaus"), from 1903 to 1905, the year in which the [*Annus Mirabilis* papers](/wiki/Annus_Mirabilis_papers "Annus Mirabilis papers") were published.

The Rose Garden (*Rosengarten*), from which a scenic panoramic view of the medieval town centre can be enjoyed, is a well-kept Rosarium on a hill, converted into a park from a former cemetery in 1913.

There are [eleven Renaissance allegorical statues](/wiki/List_of_fountains_in_Bern "List of fountains in Bern") on public fountains in the Old Town. Nearly all the 16th-century fountains, except the [Zähringer fountain](/wiki/Z%C3%A4hringerbrunnen "Zähringerbrunnen"), which was created by [Hans Hiltbrand](/w/index.php?title=Hans_Hiltbrand&action=edit&redlink=1 "Hans Hiltbrand (page does not exist)"), are the work of the [Fribourg](/wiki/Fribourg "Fribourg") master [Hans Gieng](/wiki/Hans_Gieng "Hans Gieng"). One of the more interesting fountains is the [Kindlifresserbrunnen](/wiki/Kindlifresserbrunnen "Kindlifresserbrunnen") (Bernese German: *Child Eater Fountain* ), which is claimed to represent a Jew,^[\[45\]](#cite_note-51)^ the Greek god [Chronos](/wiki/Chronos "Chronos"), or a [Fastnacht](/wiki/Swabian-Alemannic-Fastnacht "Swabian-Alemannic-Fastnacht") figure meant to frighten disobedient children.^[\[46\]](#cite_note-52)^{#cite_ref-52}

Bern's most recent sight is the set of fountains in front of the Federal Palace. It was inaugurated on 1 August 2004.

The [Universal Postal Union](/wiki/Universal_Postal_Union "Universal Postal Union") is situated in Bern.
[![](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/87/The_Zytglogge_clock_tower.jpg/220px-The_Zytglogge_clock_tower.jpg)](/wiki/File:The_Zytglogge_clock_tower.jpg) The [Zytglogge](/wiki/Zytglogge "Zytglogge") clock tower and the city's medieval covered shopping promenades (*Lauben*)  

### Heritage sites of national significance {#Heritage_sites_of_national_significance}

\[[edit](/w/index.php?title=Bern&action=edit&section=21 "Edit section: Heritage sites of national significance")\]

Bern is home to 114 Swiss [heritage sites of national significance](/wiki/Swiss_inventory_of_cultural_property_of_national_and_regional_significance "Swiss inventory of cultural property of national and regional significance").^[\[47\]](#cite_note-53)^{#cite_ref-53}

It includes the entire [Old Town](/wiki/Old_Town_of_Bern "Old Town of Bern"), which is also a UNESCO World Heritage Site, and many sites within and around it. Some of the most notable in the Old Town include the [Cathedral](/wiki/Bern_Minster "Bern Minster") which was started in 1421 and is the tallest cathedral in Switzerland, the [Zytglogge](/wiki/Zytglogge "Zytglogge") and [Käfigturm](/wiki/K%C3%A4figturm "Käfigturm") towers, which mark two successive expansions of the Old Town, and the [Holy Ghost Church](/wiki/Church_of_the_Holy_Ghost,_Bern "Church of the Holy Ghost, Bern"), which is one of the largest [Swiss Reformed](/wiki/Swiss_Reformed_Church "Swiss Reformed Church") churches in Switzerland. Within the Old Town, there are eleven [16th-century fountains](/wiki/List_of_fountains_in_Bern "List of fountains in Bern"), most attributed to [Hans Gieng](/wiki/Hans_Gieng "Hans Gieng"), that are on the list.

Outside the Old Town the heritage sites include the Bärengraben, the [Gewerbeschule Bern](/w/index.php?title=Gewerbeschule_Bern&action=edit&redlink=1 "Gewerbeschule Bern (page does not exist)") (1937), the [Eidgenössisches Archiv für Denkmalpflege](/w/index.php?title=Eidgen%C3%B6ssisches_Archiv_f%C3%BCr_Denkmalpflege&action=edit&redlink=1 "Eidgenössisches Archiv für Denkmalpflege (page does not exist)"), the [Kirchenfeld mansion district](/w/index.php?title=Kirchenfeld,_Bern&action=edit&redlink=1 "Kirchenfeld, Bern (page does not exist)") \[[de](https://de.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kirchenfeld_(Bern) "de:Kirchenfeld (Bern)")\] (after 1881), the [Thunplatzbrunnen](/w/index.php?title=Thunplatzbrunnen&action=edit&redlink=1 "Thunplatzbrunnen (page does not exist)"), the [Federal Mint](/wiki/Swissmint "Swissmint") building, the [Federal Archives](/wiki/Swiss_Federal_Archives "Swiss Federal Archives"), the [Swiss National Library](/wiki/Swiss_National_Library "Swiss National Library"), the [Historical Museum](/wiki/Historical_Museum_of_Bern "Historical Museum of Bern") (1894), [Alpine Museum](/w/index.php?title=Alpine_Museum_of_Bern&action=edit&redlink=1 "Alpine Museum of Bern (page does not exist)"), [Museum of Communication](/wiki/Museum_of_Communication_Bern "Museum of Communication Bern") and [Natural History Museum](/wiki/Natural_History_Museum_of_Bern "Natural History Museum of Bern").

------------------

### Cinemas {#Cinemas}

\[[edit](/w/index.php?title=Bern&action=edit&section=24 "Edit section: Cinemas")\]

Bern has several dozen cinemas. As is customary in German Switzerland, films are generally in German. Some films in select cinemas are shown in their original language with German and French subtitles.  

### Film festivals {#Film_festivals}

\[[edit](/w/index.php?title=Bern&action=edit&section=25 "Edit section: Film festivals")\]

* [shnit International Shortfilmfestival](/wiki/Shnit_international_shortfilmfestival "Shnit international shortfilmfestival"), held annually in early October.
* [Queersicht](/wiki/Queersicht "Queersicht") -- gay and lesbian film festival, held annually in the second week of November.

* [Gurtenfestival](/wiki/Gurtenfestival "Gurtenfestival")
* Internationales Jazzfestival Bern
* Taktlos-Festival

### Music events {#Music_events}

\[[edit](/w/index.php?title=Bern&action=edit&section=27 "Edit section: Music events")\]

The *Musikpreis des Kantons Bern* is an annual musical event where "Outstanding musicians which styles shape the Bern music scene" are honored.^[\[53\]](#cite_note-59)^^[\[54\]](#cite_note-60)^{#cite_ref-60}  

### Fairs {#Fairs}

\[[edit](/w/index.php?title=Bern&action=edit&section=28 "Edit section: Fairs")\]

* [Zibelemärit](/wiki/Zibelem%C3%A4rit "Zibelemärit") -- The Zibelemärit (onion market) is an annual fair held on the fourth Monday in November.
* [Bernese Fasnacht (Carnival)](/wiki/Bernese_Fasnacht_(Carnival) "Bernese Fasnacht (Carnival)")

Sports {#Sports}
----------------

\[[edit](/w/index.php?title=Bern&action=edit&section=29 "Edit section: Sports")\]
[![](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f9/Stade_de_Suisse_Luftbild_2011.jpg/220px-Stade_de_Suisse_Luftbild_2011.jpg)](/wiki/File:Stade_de_Suisse_Luftbild_2011.jpg) [Stadion Wankdorf](/wiki/Stadion_Wankdorf "Stadion Wankdorf")

Bern was the site of the [1954 FIFA World Cup Final](/wiki/1954_FIFA_World_Cup_Final "1954 FIFA World Cup Final"), in which [West Germany](/wiki/West_Germany_national_football_team "West Germany national football team") upset the Hungarian [Golden Team](/wiki/Golden_Team "Golden Team") 3--2. The football team [BSC Young Boys](/wiki/BSC_Young_Boys "BSC Young Boys") is based in Bern at the [Stadion Wankdorf](/wiki/Stadion_Wankdorf "Stadion Wankdorf"), which also was one of the venues for the [2008 UEFA European Championship](/wiki/UEFA_Euro_2008 "UEFA Euro 2008"), in which it hosted three matches.

[FC Breitenrain Bern](/wiki/FC_Breitenrain_Bern "FC Breitenrain Bern"), founded in 1994, also play in Bern.^[\[55\]](#cite_note-61)^{#cite_ref-61}

[SC Bern](/wiki/SC_Bern "SC Bern") is the major ice hockey team of Bern which plays in the [PostFinance Arena](/wiki/PostFinance_Arena "PostFinance Arena"). They compete in the [National League](/wiki/National_League_(ice_hockey) "National League (ice hockey)") (NL), the highest league in Switzerland. The team has ranked highest in attendance for a European hockey team for more than a decade.^[\[56\]](#cite_note-SCBernAttendence-62)^ PostFinance Arena was the main host of the [2009 IIHF Ice Hockey World Championship](/wiki/2009_IIHF_World_Championship "2009 IIHF World Championship"), including the opening game and the final of the tournament.{#cite_ref-SCBernAttendence_62-0}

PostFinance Arena was also the host of the 2011 European Figure Skate Championships.

[Bern Cardinals](/w/index.php?title=Bern_Cardinals&action=edit&redlink=1 "Bern Cardinals (page does not exist)") is the [baseball](/wiki/Baseball "Baseball") and [softball](/wiki/Softball "Softball") team of Bern, which plays at the Allmend.

Bern Grizzlies is the [American football](/wiki/American_football "American football") club in Bern (since 1985) and plays in the top level [Nationalliga A (American football)](/wiki/Nationalliga_A_(American_football) "Nationalliga A (American football)") at Athletics Arena Wankdorf. The Grizzlies have been [Swiss Bowl](/wiki/Swiss_Bowl "Swiss Bowl") champion six times.

Bern was a candidate to host the 2010 Winter Olympics, but withdrew its bid in September 2002 after a referendum was passed that showed that the bid was not supported by locals. Those games were eventually awarded to [Vancouver, British Columbia](/wiki/Vancouver "Vancouver").

RC Bern is the local rugby club (since 1972) and plays at the Allmend. The ladies team was founded in 1995.

The locality of Bremgartenwald was home to the [Bremgarten Circuit](/wiki/Bremgarten_Circuit "Bremgarten Circuit"), the [Grand Prix motor racing](/wiki/Grand_Prix_motor_racing "Grand Prix motor racing") course that at one time hosted the [Swiss Grand Prix](/wiki/Swiss_Grand_Prix "Swiss Grand Prix").

[Bern Bears](/w/index.php?title=Bern_Bears&action=edit&redlink=1 "Bern Bears (page does not exist)") is an NGO Basketball Club since 2010 in city of Bern.^[\[57\]](#cite_note-63)^{#cite_ref-63}

The [Swiss Grand Prix](/wiki/Swiss_Grand_Prix "Swiss Grand Prix") was held on the [Circuit Bremgarten](/wiki/Circuit_Bremgarten "Circuit Bremgarten") street track from 1950 to 1954, with [MotoGP](/wiki/MotoGP "MotoGP") also running their [Swiss motorcycle Grand Prix](/wiki/Swiss_motorcycle_Grand_Prix "Swiss motorcycle Grand Prix") from 1949 to 1954. The circuit eventually fell into disrepair after Switzerland banned motorsports after the [1955 Le Mans Disaster](/wiki/1955_Le_Mans_disaster "1955 Le Mans disaster"), but they made an amendment in 2015 to host electric racing, which is how the [Swiss ePrix](/wiki/Swiss_ePrix "Swiss ePrix") happened in 2019.  

Economy {#Economy}
------------------

\[[edit](/w/index.php?title=Bern&action=edit&section=30 "Edit section: Economy")\]

As of 2010^[\[update\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Bern&action=edit)^, Bern had an unemployment rate of 3.3%. As of 2008^[\[update\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Bern&action=edit)^, there were 259 people employed in the [primary economic sector](/wiki/Primary_sector_of_the_economy "Primary sector of the economy") and about 59 businesses involved in this sector. 16,413 people were employed in the [secondary sector](/wiki/Secondary_sector_of_the_economy "Secondary sector of the economy") and there were 950 businesses in this sector. 135,973 people were employed in the [tertiary sector](/wiki/Tertiary_sector_of_the_economy "Tertiary sector of the economy"), with 7,654 businesses in this sector.^[\[38\]](#cite_note-SFSO-44)^{#cite_ref-SFSO_44-5}

In 2008^[\[update\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Bern&action=edit)^ the total number of [full-time equivalent](/wiki/Full-time_equivalent "Full-time equivalent") jobs was 125,037. The number of jobs in the primary sector was 203, of which 184 were in agriculture and 19 were in forestry or lumber production. The number of jobs in the secondary sector was 15,476 of which 7,650 or (49.4%) were in manufacturing, 51 or (0.3%) were in mining and 6,389 (41.3%) were in construction. The number of jobs in the tertiary sector was 109,358. In the tertiary sector; 11,396 or 10.4% were in wholesale or retail sales or the repair of motor vehicles, 10,293 or 9.4% were in the movement and storage of goods, 5,090 or 4.7% were in a hotel or restaurant, 7,302 or 6.7% were in the information industry, 8,437 or 7.7% were the insurance or financial industry, 10,660 or 9.7% were technical professionals or scientists, 5,338 or 4.9% were in education and 17,903 or 16.4% were in health care.^[\[58\]](#cite_note-64)^{#cite_ref-64}

In 2000^[\[update\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Bern&action=edit)^, there were 94,367 workers who commuted into the municipality and 16,424 workers who commuted away. The municipality is a net importer of workers, with about 5.7 workers entering the municipality for every one leaving.^[\[59\]](#cite_note-commuter-65)^ Of the working population, 50.6% used public transport to get to work, and 20.6% used a private car.^[\[38\]](#cite_note-SFSO-44)^{#cite_ref-SFSO_44-6}  

Education {#Education}
----------------------

\[[edit](/w/index.php?title=Bern&action=edit&section=31 "Edit section: Education")\]
[![](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9b/Universit%C3%A4t_Bern_Hauptgeb%C3%A4ude_DSC05758.jpg/220px-Universit%C3%A4t_Bern_Hauptgeb%C3%A4ude_DSC05758.jpg)](/wiki/File:Universit%C3%A4t_Bern_Hauptgeb%C3%A4ude_DSC05758.jpg) Main building of the University of Bern

The [University of Bern](/wiki/University_of_Bern "University of Bern"), whose buildings are mainly located in the *Länggasse* quarter, is located in Bern, as well as the [University of Applied Sciences](/wiki/Bern_University_of_Applied_Sciences "Bern University of Applied Sciences") (*Fachhochschule*) and several vocations schools.

In Bern, about 50,418 or (39.2%) of the population have completed non-mandatory [upper secondary education](/wiki/Education_in_Switzerland#Secondary "Education in Switzerland"), and 24,311 or (18.9%) have completed additional higher education (either [university](/wiki/List_of_universities_in_Switzerland "List of universities in Switzerland") or a *[Fachhochschule](/wiki/Fachhochschule "Fachhochschule")* ). Of the 24,311 who completed tertiary schooling, 51.6% were Swiss men, 33.0% were Swiss women, 8.9% were non-Swiss men and 6.5% were non-Swiss women.^[\[39\]](#cite_note-STAT2000-45)^{#cite_ref-STAT2000_45-4}

The canton of Bern school system provides one year of non-obligatory [kindergarten](/wiki/Kindergarten "Kindergarten"), followed by six years of primary school. This is followed by three years of obligatory lower secondary school where the pupils are separated according to ability and aptitude. Following the lower secondary pupils may attend additional schooling or they may enter an [apprenticeship](/wiki/Apprenticeship "Apprenticeship").^[\[60\]](#cite_note-66)^{#cite_ref-66}

During the 2009--10 school year, there were a total of 10,979 pupils attending classes in Bern. There were 89 kindergarten classes with a total of 1,641 pupils in the municipality. Of the kindergarten pupils, 32.4% were permanent or temporary residents of Switzerland (not citizens) and 40.2% have a different mother language than the classroom language. The municipality had 266 primary classes and 5,040 pupils. Of the primary pupils, 30.1% were permanent or temporary residents of Switzerland (not citizens) and 35.7% have a different mother language than the classroom language. During the same year, there were 151 lower secondary classes with a total of 2,581 pupils. There were 28.7% who were permanent or temporary residents of Switzerland (not citizens) and 32.7% have a different mother language than the classroom language.^[\[61\]](#cite_note-School-67)^{#cite_ref-School_67-0}

Notable schools in Bern include [Gymnasium Neufeld](/wiki/Gymnasium_Neufeld "Gymnasium Neufeld").

Bern is home to 8 libraries. These libraries include; the Schweiz. Nationalbibliothek/ Bibliothèque nationale suisse, the *Universitätsbibliothek Bern* , the *Kornhausbibliotheken Bern* , the *BFH Wirtschaft und Verwaltung Bern* , the *BFH Gesundheit* , the *BFH Soziale Arbeit* , the *Hochschule der Künste Bern, Gestaltung und Kunst* and the *Hochschule der Künste Bern, Musikbibliothek* . There was a combined total (as of 2008^[\[update\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Bern&action=edit)^) of 10,308,336 books or other media in the libraries, and in the same year a total of 2,627,973 items were loaned out.^[\[62\]](#cite_note-68)^{#cite_ref-68}

As of 2000^[\[update\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Bern&action=edit)^, there were 9,045 pupils in Bern who came from another municipality, while 1,185 residents attended schools outside the municipality.^[\[59\]](#cite_note-commuter-65)^{#cite_ref-commuter_65-1}  

Transport {#Transport}
----------------------

\[[edit](/w/index.php?title=Bern&action=edit&section=32 "Edit section: Transport")\]
[![](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/87/Bern_tram_and_cathedral.png/220px-Bern_tram_and_cathedral.png)](/wiki/File:Bern_tram_and_cathedral.png) [Tram](/wiki/Trams_in_Bern "Trams in Bern") on the Kirchenfeldbrücke, with the [Bern Minster](/wiki/Bern_Minster "Bern Minster") and Casino Bern in the background  
Main articles: [BERNMOBIL](/wiki/BERNMOBIL "BERNMOBIL"), [Trams in Bern](/wiki/Trams_in_Bern "Trams in Bern"), [Trolleybuses in Bern](/wiki/Trolleybuses_in_Bern "Trolleybuses in Bern"), and [Bern S-Bahn](/wiki/Bern_S-Bahn "Bern S-Bahn")  

### Public transport {#Public_transport}

\[[edit](/w/index.php?title=Bern&action=edit&section=33 "Edit section: Public transport")\]

Bern is served by a dense network of trains, [trams](/wiki/Trams_in_Bern "Trams in Bern"), [trolleybuses](/wiki/Trolleybuses_in_Bern "Trolleybuses in Bern"), and conventional motorbuses. The [Bern S-Bahn](/wiki/Bern_S-Bahn "Bern S-Bahn") is Switzerland's second busiest.

Bern is the centre of the [Libero tariff network](/wiki/Libero-Tarifverbund "Libero-Tarifverbund"), which covers the cantons of Bern and [Solothurn](/wiki/Canton_of_Solothurn "Canton of Solothurn") and includes the towns of [Biel/Bienne](/wiki/Biel/Bienne "Biel/Bienne"), [Solothurn](/wiki/Solothurn "Solothurn"), and [Thun](/wiki/Thun "Thun"). The network allows easy and coordinated travel on all modes of public transport, such as trains, [PostAuto buses](/wiki/PostBus_Switzerland "PostBus Switzerland"), [trams](/wiki/Trams_in_Bern "Trams in Bern"), buses ([trolleybuses](/wiki/Trolleybuses_in_Bern "Trolleybuses in Bern") and motorbuses) and others, regardless of transport operator. Fares are based on the number of zones in a journey. The central part of Bern, (excluding *[Bümpliz](/wiki/B%C3%BCmpliz "Bümpliz")* , *Betlehem* , *Bottigen* , *Brünnen* , and *Riedbach* in the west of the municipality), is part of the fare zone *100*.
[![](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9d/Bern_Hauptbahnhof_%282014%29.jpg/220px-Bern_Hauptbahnhof_%282014%29.jpg)](/wiki/File:Bern_Hauptbahnhof_(2014).jpg) [Bern railway station](/wiki/Bern_railway_station "Bern railway station")

The city is well served by railways, with the extensive S-Bahn network and many regional and international connections. [Bern's central railway station](/wiki/Bern_railway_station "Bern railway station") (*Bahnhof Bern* ) is Switzerland's second busiest station (164,800 passengers per weekday in 2022), and is the main transport hub in the region.^[\[63\]](#cite_note-69)^{#cite_ref-69}

A [funicular railway](/wiki/Funicular_railway "Funicular railway") called the [Marzilibahn](/wiki/Marzili_Funicular "Marzili Funicular") leads from the *Marzili* district to the [Federal Palace](/wiki/Federal_Palace_of_Switzerland "Federal Palace of Switzerland"). With a length of 106 m (348 ft), it is the second shortest public railway in Europe after the [Zagreb funicular](/wiki/Zagreb_funicular "Zagreb funicular").  

### Road traffic {#Road_traffic}

\[[edit](/w/index.php?title=Bern&action=edit&section=34 "Edit section: Road traffic")\]

[Several Aare bridges](/wiki/List_of_Aar_bridges_in_Bern "List of Aar bridges in Bern") connect the old parts of the city with the newer districts outside of the peninsula.

Bern is well connected to other cities by several [motorways](/wiki/Autobahns_of_Switzerland "Autobahns of Switzerland") ([A1](/wiki/A1_(Switzerland) "A1 (Switzerland)"), [A12](/wiki/A12_motorway_(Switzerland) "A12 motorway (Switzerland)"), [A6](/wiki/A6_motorway_(Switzerland) "A6 motorway (Switzerland)")).  

### Airport {#Airport}

\[[edit](/w/index.php?title=Bern&action=edit&section=35 "Edit section: Airport")\]

[Bern Airport](/wiki/Bern_Airport "Bern Airport") (colloquially called *Bern-Belp* or *Belpmoos* ) located outside the city near the town of [Belp](/wiki/Belp "Belp"), as of March 2021 mostly serves [general aviation](/wiki/General_aviation "General aviation") and charter flights. [Zurich Airport](/wiki/Zurich_Airport "Zurich Airport"), [Geneva Airport](/wiki/Geneva_Airport "Geneva Airport") and [EuroAirport Basel Mulhouse Freiburg](/wiki/EuroAirport_Basel_Mulhouse_Freiburg "EuroAirport Basel Mulhouse Freiburg") serve as gateways for air traffic, all reachable in less than two hours by [train](/wiki/SBB_CFF_FFS "SBB CFF FFS") or car from Bern.  

### Bicycle transport {#Bicycle_transport}

\[[edit](/w/index.php?title=Bern&action=edit&section=36 "Edit section: Bicycle transport")\]

The city has made efforts to make Bern the "bicycle capital" of Switzerland through the creation of better infrastructure, such as dedicated cycle paths.^[\[64\]](#cite_note-70)^ [PubliBike](/w/index.php?title=PubliBike&action=edit&redlink=1 "PubliBike (page does not exist)") \[[de](https://de.wikipedia.org/wiki/PubliBike "de:PubliBike")\] operates a bike-sharing system.{#cite_ref-70}
